And if there are fistulas that penetrate just to the bladder, and just to the middle of the rod; and they extend just to the joint of the thigh, and just to the top of the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one recognizes the fistula penetrating to the foundation, and not piercing through:
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and it is that you apply your indexed finger to the foundation, and insert a subtle needle of iron or silver into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is twisting, you insert a subtle probe of lead, or a horsehair, as long as you feel the probe or hair at your finger.
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and it does not come from a sharp perturbation or evacuation, nor from wind, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	know that it does not penetrate deeply; thus you hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is close to the bladder or close to the urinary tract, then the urine jumps, and cannot be soothed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is perceived close to the joint of the hip, then the tense vein comes close to the place;
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	If there is no twisting and the discovery of pain inward, it is that it is always thus bowed, and there is no medicine that can be suddenly applied by pricking.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these persistent fistulas there is no cure except through effort, and vanity of foolish remedies that get in the way.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In one that is not persistent and not ancient, there is hope of health through iron, as I have experienced.
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and it is that the patient places himself between your hands on his back; and he lifts his legs up to his hips, and has his hips inclined towards his stomach;
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	Then apply a tent of thread, or of lead if there is torsion, until you know where the thread comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the patient feels it at the foundation, then it is necessary that you apply your right index finger,
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	Then sense that the thread has penetrated; and so discover where you feel between your finger the siphac or the flesh, then know that it is perforating.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If you do not work on it, one cannot heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	One cannot completely heal all wounds, but it happens rarely;
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the aid that one does, if it is that one heats the subtle cautery according to the size of the fistula, as it has been said before;
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and insert the hot iron into the fistula, until it reaches the bottom; and do this two or three times, as long as you know that these hardened crusts are burned, which resemble a bird's feather;
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then treat the tender moist areas with powder, until those crusts are dry, then treat with ointment, soothing and closing the wound.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If he is thus healthy, it’s good. If he does not have it, another way cannot make him healthy;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and hold it between, and do not prick exactly to the finger which is at the foundation, and between your finger and the holder a thick covering of flesh or of skin, and you see the fistula at that which follows the covering of the vein;
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if you cut from the beginning of the fistula, and thrust before the holder, and then apply the cautery, until it reaches the head of the holder;
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	and the holder will be delivered, and fall; then I will show you those worn-out flesh that seem like a bird's feather, and none of them will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the wound is swollen, and it forms a crust between the skin and the vein, then cauterize with fire or medicine water.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For the fire cauterizes assemble many things: it is to know, the burning of these joined flesh, and the staunching of blood and the drying of moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then the treatment of swollen limbs in mud or in a broken box, as long as the blood flows freely, and it makes the burnt flesh open in the mud;
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then treat the wound of the swollen fingers with a dry poultice made from hard charcoal, and these are the dry medications.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, then it is healthy and does not relapse again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes just to the edge of the foundation, and is separated from the body, then you should apply your finger or foundation, and inquire about it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the tension, and between two is the cloth or the suture or flesh, or it is near to piercing, if there are not more ways than the way of faith and hope, through the administration of one of the three manners:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	where you cauterize as we have said, or you cut just to the base, or if you can place tente and cure as before.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too deeply into the marrow, lest you pierce the tendons that hold the foundation, and come to the gestures by the deliberate sense.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then the treatment, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	by chance if it will be healthy, or you remove that covering and the bundle, then it is cut from the deep foundation, either by tension or by another appointed instrument;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then I will show you that faulty flesh which is in the wound, as much as you can;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then study how to restore the wound, and to stop the fistula in the part that is opposite the foundation: if it is easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And often fistulas are treated in this manner: and it is when you push the tent into the fistula, and it is where the foundation of the wound is beneath the skin above.
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	if you take a perforated tent according to this form at the head:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And you push a twisted thread into it, and push the tent onto all the threads in the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is deeply embedded in the margin of the wound, then extract the thread of the affected part, so that you touch your finger or base;
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	and draw the head of the thread, and join the two heads together, and hold one to the other, and let it stay for a day or two;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and restrain it no more, until the threads consume these flesh that are between them, and heal;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then treat the wound until it is sewn and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not penetrate, then make it penetrate in all ways that you can, if it is not too deep inside.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not suit to make a copper setting in the depth, and then the treatment, as we have said, until it is healthy.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the spine-like fistula that one makes if it is very narrow at one end and cutting.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and not on the other part, because one should not cut what one should not cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of the bruises
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Bruises are of two kinds: either they are deep in the foundation, like a grain of resin, and there are small and large ones, and they immediately stop the blood flow.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	and there is one or more, and they are deep in the foundation and at the head of the foundation; but those that are deep have little moisture,
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and immediately stop or a little yellowish water or a little blood, and they have the color of the body.
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment of those who have them in the foundation, if it is that you instruct the patient to stretch out for walking in chambers, until the foundations issue forth, and appear the threads;
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you hurry, and hold it like a bandage, or you hold it on your finger, then cut it at its roots;
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the uncle cannot hold them due to moisture, take them with a strip of cloth, or a ribbon, or a piece of chamelot;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and stretch them to your fingers, then cut them, and sprinkle above some warm powders that are in the vein of cautery;
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	where you cauterize as it is said in the chapter of cauterization, then heal with other treatments until they are healthy;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundations cannot issue forth, then cleanse the patient of piercing and bitter clusters by washing what is in the foundation, so that it may issue forth openly;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	when the patients cannot take it, and if the veins are far from the foundation, then the treatment is light;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and it is that you take them to your finger or to the nails, and you cut, then you treat as we have said, until they are healthy, and that they fear the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	Here is the translation:
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and it is very loose; and hold the thread firmly, then pinch the thread, and extract the needle, and do thus with all the others, and leave them there for correcting the excessive bleeding.
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put on the dressing, a piece of cloth soaked in rose oil or cerate, and put it on the base, and instruct the patient to rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then leave it until it heals, and when they will be healed, if you treat with ointment and other treatments, until they are healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the dryness of the veins or base
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Here is the translation:
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	It is necessary that you hold the point of a spatula or on one nail the scab over, which does not allow it to become damp.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then heal it as soon as it is dry so as it is necessary.
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot be dried, then restart the rubbing more forcefully than before, until it bleeds much and is scarified.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal it as soon as it is healthy.
dou fremit	you apply heat
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Formica is a small, swollen appearance that goes against the body, and it eats much in depth;
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and often one finds the frost, and it feels just like death from heat, and it comes to all the body, and more in the hands than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the treatment is that you take a small thread of an eagle's feather, or a strong vulture's feather, and put that thread on the heat, so that the circles surround the heat entirely.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand to the whole cane as you grasp everything around the arm, and put it in the foreground, and strip the arm of its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make a cane of iron or steel in this form, and be subtle below and draw above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce, because you must hold with your finger, and press; And if you see, cauterize the arm, as it is before or in a chapter of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the cluster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never make a cluster of silver or copper, or tin alloy or chain mail; and never make use of these small and large instruments, according to the ones that are at hand.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	These therefore that one uses in the treatment of children who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the small and large cluster is above large, or the belly is tied according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and there is a separation or the belly is tied, as you see, and the chest is perceived within; and has on one side a perforated opening, and on the other a perforated opening.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and it be the belly or womb where one puts medicines of a bladder of beast or of parchment, and it be pierced all around with small holes,
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and have between each hole a thread of space, then insert into these holes strong thread strongly twisted in X or around, and assemble the belly as if it were a sack;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, then tie it to the instrument in front of a strong thread, then cleanse; and that's the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine be not too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clistere with oil or apple juice, or similar thing, then insert it lightly;
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	Then the minister's fingers are applied to his joined hands, so that they be completely visible, then the cluster is removed, and the patient lifts his legs to the bench.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if the medicine wants to issue, then the bandage as much as he can; and if he sleeps a night entirely, it is more great aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you clusterize him in illness of bowel disorder, and the medicine hastens to issue, then recommend it as much as he be healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are at the foundation, or abscess, then let the cluster be as subtly applied as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and it is the subtle form of the cluster held steady on the skin:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken about the treatment of wounds in the division; now we will tell you about manual and medical treatments, according to the fulfillment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the locations or places where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	Here is the translation:
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	where they are made according to the laws of the body, as if a wound is situated on the neck, or on the head, or the feet, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, for the remedy will come to its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it is a judgment of stone or similar things, and the skin is entirely ruined and the wound is great,
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you doubt the vehement aposteme heat: if you make it healthier from the cephalic membrane at once, so that it comes little blood from the wound, and let the health be contrary to the naval part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and abstain the patient from repletion of wine and of coarse meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to recover, let his meat be diminished, and do not drink any wine, nor eat any flesh.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and apply to the wound, a poultice made with hot oil rose soothingly, or with wine stippled.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot abscess, apply to the wound, so that it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by the air, powder, which I will tell a little about later.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and he arms it moves, if you put on some ointments, as long as it is healthy.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be assembled by stretching, if they are assembled by stitching, as I will say about wounds of the belly, from the stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is discovered in the bone, and it is deep, and holds no more than a little, if you probe; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard skin in place of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	and instruct the patient to eat thick foods, as if they are tested and cooked well, like roasted poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find a skin lesion, and it does not adhere to the bone, so scrape off all the putrid flesh, and apply a dressing, then treat.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if it has entered into the wound or vein, without a crust, and it cannot be staunched by medicines, so seek out the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it off with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if that does not benefit, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and it is that you apply this powder which soothes thus that the arsenic has moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of the powder is: take encense in one part; blood of dragon two parts; lively chalk three parts, and subtly grind the powder.
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply the plaster, and hold it firmly in place, until it adheres well and joins to all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then bind it well, and leave it without loosening, so it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And at no time does one make a poultice of chalk solely, when one has not the encense nor the blood of dragon, but rather the arsenic has not moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the artery has moved away from the wound, meanwhile it is in this state, if you do not put this powder.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but apply some digestive ointments, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it casts off the pus.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat other wounds as long as they are healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the fracture of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with subtle pinches.
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you about the breaks of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is on the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it's the nerves, there is no other remedy than to leave the cure, and not to put anything constricting, for it harms the nerves and makes them retract.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the essence of nerves is cold, and its continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member;
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but let the medicines be soothing, as if you warm the water in sweet oil, and mix it with rose oil, and cook the water thus in sweet oil,
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other remedies of mine according to this method, and moist applications.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, sew it up with bands, then treat it until it is healthy.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and it is hairy and full of pus, prick there or lower down;
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut, and a stream of blood comes, then stop it, and bind it, and cauterize, for this is his profession;
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	and if the spinal cord of the throat is cut, or the knees, and the conduits are guarded, because that's where the food goes,
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	if you cut the knee on the vein of the throat, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape;
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then hold it firmly, and let it rest for some days, then heal the wounds completely so that they are healthy;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, so to speak;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are fragments of bone, remove them gently so you can, and those that you cannot have, let them be until the wound putrefies;
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and clear away and align the discharge;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, then powder on the powder that I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has become fistulous, then the treatment should be as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	from a wound of a spear or a knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a blow of a spear or a knife, and the wound is deep, then examine if the wound has become putrid, as soon as the patient complains: know then that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it is not deep, and it is fresh in all its blood, then do not put the powder at the first hour, nor bind it with a bandage that does not stop the bleeding.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and return to the body, and open the affected part;
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but I put an attractive ointment, and bind it with a bandage several times a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you have no ointment, put much cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture,
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and have the patient sleep on the wound for two days, or three days, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if there is no spasm coming, nor evil trembling of heart nor signs of anguish;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see the good dispositions, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Heal the wounds with tents and other treatments, as long as they are healthy;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if she cannot heal, and operate, then know that there is a fistula; if the treatment is as one must do it.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, or in the chest or back, then treat what is in front.
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	if it is large, of stitching; and if it is small, of powder, and if it is pressed into the bone, and has caught pieces, then cauterize the wound, and remove the excess flesh if they are decayed.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not decayed, then let the wound rot, if you alleviate the extractions.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and of other wounds to other limbs is the judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	Here is the translation:
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The rupture of the belly is great and moderate and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from the great wound sometimes the intestine, or the ends of the intestines, because of the introversion of them;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the stitching is more troublesome, and sometimes it is better to have a small wound than a large one;
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	because when we put the intestines back in place, we must not reinsert them from hot to hot;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	Because the intestines swell so much that they feel cold, if they retract more to points,
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and because it makes the moist wound worse, because one must reset the intestine to its place like the others.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is in three ways:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the common ruptures have a rupture of the belly,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the treatment of other wounds of the body and other proper treatments are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and they are even more proper with the treatment of the belly, and I will tell each one and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the intestine is outside,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and grievous things are to be reset, it is by one of the aforementioned methods:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	for the smallness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	because the intestine is swollen from the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is chilled, warm it up in such a way:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	soak a sponge or a piece of cloth in hot water, then apply it gently,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	where you burn with a pointed iron and sprinkle and pierce,
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and raise the intestine until the inflammation is removed;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and many times they make these constricted veins, and it is murderous that they should be relieved of inflammation.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the inflammation departing, then anoint the intestine with hot water or warm milk and bad humors are cured,
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	because it is aligned with the entrance to a little thing;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a little wound at the instrument through which one gathers the blood vessels;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first treatment is to remove what is superfluous;
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	for we must not cut without great necessity, lest it harm;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and it's the instruments for the splitting:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if you cut deeply into the curve and do not deviate, and see there the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine bursts out,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	if you put it back in its natural shape in its proper place,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	Here is the translation:
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is large, and it is on the lower part of the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	it is necessary that you lay the patient on his back,
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and place his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and it is in the lower part of the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	Place the finger and the foot higher than the parts below.
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and thus the rupture of the belly is in one of the injured parts.
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	if you find that the injured part is higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to administer what I say in great and minor wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	Small wounds heal when that which is prepared for you appears.
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then they are in your hands, I, a pitiful minister who draws the entire route to his hand,
et assemble les levres;	and bring together the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and it is the common manner of stitches,
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and it is that you take a needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave at the head of the wound, I do not spare, and I fix a needle or it has a strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the skin with the skin of the siphal,
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is beneath the skin within, so that you make it pierce from that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and gather the main wound from which the abscesses burst forth;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then strain with a double thread within the needle of the wound, through,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then gather the heads of the wounds that are about to open,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then let it be touched by the space, and fix another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then thread the lively file as you did the first needle
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not cease from doing that, according to what you have mastered of the needles
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until the entire wound is restrained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and let the needles be moderate, between subtle and large,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	because the subtle needles grasp all the flesh, and those too gross cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	for it is necessary that they be ground;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and it is not necessary to push the needles too far into the depth of the flesh and soft skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	so that they grasp and open the wound before the suture;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then cut the heads of the veins so they do not bother the patient while sleeping,
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I hold tight or wrap around the heads of the veins to keep them steady,
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and let them be until the wound is sewn;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this method of cutting the veins is more suitable for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	for he suffers from a needle or .ij.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second wound is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is that you gather the .ij. heads of skin and the .ij. heads of soft tissue together with a needle or he has a strong thread in the middle;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced these heads all together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	If you reset the needle to the part where you began, in the manner that one cuts the threads;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and place a space between each stitch the thickness of a smaller finger;
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitching follows the bone,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I treated a wound that one had in the belly or abdomen,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	who was wounded by a dagger
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm's width of great,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and it was deep into the intestines, well .ij. palms of great,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was in the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I bring back the intestine, then it has been 23 hours, for
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was sewn up to the 15th day, and it was cured, and it was healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the doctor had given up that he would die, and this was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and did not cure him with ointment, for I stayed in the place where they found none, nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and apply a moderate heat on the wound cotton cloth many times a day, and wash with warm honey water as long as it was healthy.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the proper ways of suturing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle, and sew up the part that is hurt just up to the place that is inside;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced the right heart in the right way, if you have sewn up the head of the siphac or cousteit or where you have sewn with the needle,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and have them pierce from another part of the inner section just up to the area of defeat;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the understanding of this treatment is that you sew as the pelleting maker makes the pellets,
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and that you leave once the stitching of one part, and take it up again from another, until the treatment is entirely completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second manner of treatment, which Galen says is proper,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	if it is so, like a spring which naturally assembles the disjointed parts
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and apply one head of the wound to the other head, in such a way:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	insert a needle or a pointed instrument into the wound, and make it pierce the swelling beneath,
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and let the disjointed heads of the wound
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	Then turn the needle, and make it pierce through the weakened part just up to the sensitive area within.
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	as it clears the syrupy head;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make them pierce one and the other through the weakened part just up to the sensitive area within, in the other heads of the syrupy gut that are on the other side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and it is the most common manner of stitching and the most frequent.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galens says this passage, and no one bears witness to it,
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	one must cauterize the belly with .ij. needles, or there will be a thread in each of them;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must push one needle from one side and the other from another, in the manner of those who sew up wounds;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the rupture is within the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	if it is the seam more grievous than other places of the belly wound.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgments of the other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the fresh wound in all its blood, thus showing that the artery has moved,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	then reset the intestine, and the cut; then put on the powder of engarrating charcoal,
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and he arms are swollen, if you put on any ointment that is present, as long as the wound is festering;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and cut the vein, and be careful with the skin, and the membrane;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal the wound as with the others, until it is healthy;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you have no medicines, put them on, as soon as it begins to fester badly, much cotton;
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and he moves it several times a day so it may be healthy.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you do not have mastery of another medicine in many dispositions when the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound does not affect the principal members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	then it is necessary that you apply a light bandage in oil of temperature-calming, or in rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and place them between the jaws, and beneath the seat bones;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if he feels pain or rotting in his belly, and many times it happens,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	if they administer a cluster of black wine enema, and meanwhile the rotting reaches up to the intestines;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierce it within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine that is called "fasting" cannot heal when it is wounded.
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and it's because of the delicacy of the veins that they are, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the approach to its natural condition.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the scar heals from the wound, then set it back as soon as the intestine, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and turns towards green or black, then you must read the place that is black, which removes blood that does not come from a vein.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	because there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cut what is between the vein,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put the eyes watching from the part below the wound until it befalls to alleviate the extraction when the wounds close, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	from the rupture of a broken bone
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is inflamed, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	if it can be restored in some ways,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I saw that a man was wounded or pierced in the belly by a spear;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and was inflamed and became fistulous, and thus he lost digestion and windiness;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I put a treatment according to what I could, and did not stop subtling until he was healthy, and the wounds dried up.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw him dry up, I doubted that the patient had a bad thing in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and he had no trouble, but remained in better dispositions, and eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and they direct some experimenters that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be tied up in such manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take firm hold of large thighs, then assemble the lips of the wound,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the thighs have opened their mouth, then place them on the two lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	if it stretches its mouth thus;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then he cuts off the head, and it holds so well that it cannot disjoint.
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put another ferment in the same way as before, until the wound is completely covered;
et cout la plaie.	and sew up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	That head if it gets stuck in the intestine, and does not cause any harm to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and one can bind the intestine with a subtle thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in such a manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the head of this intestine thread which should be very loosened,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie it to the head of this thread, that is a subtle twisted flaxen thread,
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Then put the thread in the needle, and sew up the intestine, and reset it in its proper route.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of stitching wounds is not fiercer than according to the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, especially when it is in one of the intestinal tubes, if there is no ingenious remedy, except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that every wound or abscess, when it becomes swollen, is universally called a "fistula".
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and similarly when it is hairy and produces a lump.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to the truth a hard, painful, and white nodulation, where one does not feel pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it is also hairy like the feather of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes in clear ulceration, and sometimes in thick scabs;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	and sometimes a little, and sometimes enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have already spoken about the classification of wounds, that every wound that is not sutured, and there is no flesh;
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	it is not otherwise except by one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	it's knowing, by the small passage of blood or course;
ou por sa malice;	or by his wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh within, and on the lips, which does not allow anything to be born of flesh;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or where there is too much swelling;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	where the lesion is putrid, and the material is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	where the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	where because the corruption is a type of plague;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	where the property in the region is slow in digestion, and slow in health, and weak by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the medical treatments in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or it is necessary that I teach you to know the treatment of fistula which is done by surgical operation with hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula occurs in all tender parts of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas that come to the great veins, and to the arteries, and to the nerves
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or to the spleen, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or to the spine of the back, or to some joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it comes to the property of the principal member, and similar things.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are of this kind are of grievous healing, and there is no remedy but labor, and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if it has any fistula that does not come near the place I have told, and you have confidence in the cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you will examine it, if you take a thin rod of iron or steel, the fistula is straight, if you want it;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is twisted, seek it with a subtle probe of lead,
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	for they fill themselves with muscles against the twistedness;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and they form a fistula at the pierced hands and you cannot well examine it by palpations,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	if you touch it with one of the pierced areas,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	for the moisture flows from one pierced area to another, and it festers;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then you recognize by your power whether there is bone or nerve, and it is shaved away in the front.
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient about the pain they feel when you press with your hand, and the place where they feel it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you truly know the place where it is, and whether it is near a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places that I have told you, if you cut according to what I have told you,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and remove for the putrid matter and the corrupt humors that are within
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then the treatment so that it may be healthy,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is well perforated in the right place, then you should cut through deeply, as much as you can,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then I apply warm compresses in medicinal agua, and the boils just at the head of the fistula,
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	as long as the medicine corrodes the excess which is remaining at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I put ointments on the wounds, so that they may be healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healthy by this, then one should cauterize as we have said,
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then one should cut.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve does not bother you with principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is uncovered, and there is decay and blackness, so let it be until the decay is entirely removed,
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal the affected things in the same way as long as they are healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healthy, and render void what was before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you are not able to heal just as they do:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	if it becomes uncovered and you strive as much as you are at the bottom,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then restore the place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healthy, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	Here is the translation:
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other remedy than to let Nature do its work;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if it has a small corrupt bone, and you can treat it with bandages,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if the extraction is done with an instrument suitable for that,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if it has many bones, so take them out three at a time, do not leave more than one;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if moisture makes you oppose, there is no error or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	if you bind and moisten and heat, and release the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, then put on the wound a poultice causing rotting,
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and let it be until the flesh is rotten among the bones,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then if they have lighter bones;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it's a large bone, such as the leg or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	if you extract so much of the corruption that the blackness is entirely removed,
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large part of the rotten corpse, it comes just to the mole of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it is necessary to sew and cover up to the corruption, and then to treat until it is healed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you of a fistula that happened to a man in his leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	if you take an example and help in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	He was a young man of around thirty years old, who had a pain in his leg due to a cause that came from within the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	until the humors went to the leg, and he was afflicted with a large abscess, and had no way of relieving himself by opening;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but his mirror showed him foolishly that they were so swollen that the abscesses opened,
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and in corroding much of the matter, and it became fistula, and many perforations occurred that all gathered together in a wound and moisture of the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many a mirror mirrored cure within these years, and there was no wisdom in the art of hands,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	until I was called, and saw his leg and the medicines with which he was treated,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and that which corrupts through the pores to a great body;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the body of the young man became red, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I burned a tent in one of these perforations, and then sought all the perforations.
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and found that some came against each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I hurried then, and cut into one of the perforations as far as I discovered a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and found it corrupt and pierced, and the corruption came just up to the bone within;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I saw those who appeared to me with a corrupt bone, and I believed there was no other corruption, except for that which I had.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to restore the wound with medicines soothing over a long period, and could not heal;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I recommenced, and discovered the bone as it was beforehand,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and found the continued corruption in the bone, and saw it, and then had it, and thought of healing the wound;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I do not touch it as much as I grasp around a palm of the bone, and the trait follows to its entire mass,
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored the administration of medicines; and it was healthy and sound immediately,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and it did not require to restart the work forcefully because of the weakness of the patient, who could not suffer,
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and for the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For because of the blood evacuation often, but he was entirely healthy.
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and a hard crust formed on the bone, and he was of good disposition and had no hindrance nor contradiction in everything, neither in going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, thus it must be treated in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	Take the ligament, and stretch it to the head of the bone that is open,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command him to stretch up high;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and put another bandage on the larger vein, and tie it above the flesh which is above the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and stretch the head, if you pull out the corrupt flesh from below,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh above the limb where you see swelling, so that the swelling does not affect the flesh;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and apply a poultice or a tablet under the bone to cover the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to clean so much that one can see and feel the corruption, and to clean again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not appear so, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	then uncover the entire flesh; then apply a poultice under,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then the putrid matter spreads from one part to another, and it is the putrid discharge of the corruption that pours out, as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut off the corrupted joint, and pour out the bone or whatever it contains from the other part;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of the joined bones, then there is no other remedy than to cut through.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is in the grasp of the hand, or in the grasp of the foot, then it is very strong that thing,
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but however it is necessary that you inquire about this decay, how it appears to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and the decaying in all the ways that you can, but that the vein or nerve does not make contrary signs to you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the incisors and the veins are for coping with these bones which are many, according to the arrangement of the bones and the appearance of the outlets,
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and their subtlety, and their greatness and their smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and therefore it is necessary to prepare each similar appearance of surgery instrument;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that the work will show you the instrument you will have need of, according to the knowledge of this art,
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the methods of illnesses;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if you prepare the instrument you will have need of, according to what is necessary for it.
dou feu	for fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head collapses either because of inwardness or because of fury;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you will have applied the medicine to that corrosion through the treatment with medicines, and it does not benefit at all,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then you must cover that member up to the place or where the corrosion comes from,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	if the patient is wounded by this of death, or by malice, which is greater, than the fault of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the limbs turn black, as if they were burned by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and afterwards the blackness spreads, then goes that corrosion of limb to limb,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and takes over the entire body; if you hasten to cure it,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and it is through the impact of certain venomous beasts, like the sea scorpion and viper and similar things,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	the corrosion is at the chief of two fingers, thus the cope, and do not give it space to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, thus the cope at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come up to the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes to the arm, thus the cope at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and it is of no use to apply remedies that are not equal to its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and thus we do when the corrosion comes or hurts: if it comes in the first joint, then it seizes after one joint and another;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes or hurts, then it seizes the whole foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it climbs up to the leg, then it seizes at the joint of the knee;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes from above the knee, there is no other remedy than to let the patient die of the wound;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the way to amputate or to saw through the limb is that you tie it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and extend one minister on one of the lower ligaments, and another minister on the other upper ligament,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you dissect the flesh that is between the two ligaments at a spacious interval, so that the bone may be uncovered;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then apply the cupping or suction, and put a piece of linen on each part, so that the suction does not touch the healthy skin.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and bring to the patient another wound and abscess ulcer.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if the flow of blood comes when you open, then cauterize the skin hastily.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	where you put on some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is accomplished.
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then he should bind the injured limb with a suitable bandage, and care for it until it is healthy;
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I would advise him that he had an injury in his own foot:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he had a black spot which seemed to be burnt by fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that corrosion came first in his toe of the foot, so that it devoured the entire foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man sees the decay, if he hastens to cover the foot, and was healthy;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long afterwards the decay returns on the hand, or on the other arm, and it comes to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put them on receptive things after the purification of the body, and could not stop the corroding;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he saw that I covered the hand, and I did not want, that I had hoped to recover the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I also fear that if he cuts his hand, it will not die
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	for the strength of the man was feeble; and he became desperate, and returned to his land
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he hastened to amputate his hand, and was cured
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have not counted it as one of those things that are done in another way, so that one has mastery.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Never does an abscess come to a head swollen with charcoal, and it stays so long that it forms a large collection of pus.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then it bursts and pierces, and the pus jumps out, and the swollen eyes become dim, just like a vessel;
